<a id="1229" class="Comment">-- Section 14.1</a>

<a id="1246" class="Comment">{- We define the type of cocones with vertex X on a span. Since we will use it
   later on, we will also characterize the identity type of the type of cocones
   with a given vertex X. -}</a>

<a id="5417" class="Comment">{- A cocone c on a span S is said to satisfy the universal property of the
   pushout of S if the function cocone-map is an equivalence for every type Y.
   -}</a>

<a id="7393" class="Comment">{- We derive a 3-for-2 property of pushouts, analogous to the 3-for-2 property
   of pullbacks. -}</a>

<a id="10875" class="Comment">{- We will assume that every span has a pushout. Moreover, we will introduce
   some further terminology to facilitate working with these pushouts. -}</a>

<a id="11027" class="Keyword">postulate</a>

<a id="16875" class="Comment">--------------------------------------------------------------------------------</a>

<a id="16957" class="Comment">-- Section 14.3 Duality of pushouts and pullbacks</a>
  
<a id="17010" class="Comment">{- The universal property of the pushout of a span S can also be stated as a
   pullback-property: a cocone c = (pair i (pair j H)) with vertex X
   satisfies the universal property of the pushout of S if and only if the
   square

     Y^X -----
``` Y^B
      |          |
      |          |
      V          V
     Y^A -----
``` Y^S

   is a pullback square for every type Y. Below, we first define the cone of
   this commuting square, and then we introduce the type 
   pullback-property-pushout, which states that the above square is a pullback.
   -}</a>

<a id="htpy-precomp"></a><a id="17568" href="synthetic-homotopy-theory.24-pushouts.html#17568" class="Function">htpy-precomp</a> <a id="17581" class="Symbol">:</a>

<a id="18689" class="Comment">{- In order to show that the universal property of pushouts is equivalent to 
   the pullback property, we show that the maps cocone-map and the gap map fit 
   in a commuting triangle, where the third map is an equivalence. The claim 
   then follows from the 3-for-2 property of equivalences. -}</a>

      <a id="21458" class="Symbol">(</a> <a id="21460" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="21461" href="synthetic-homotopy-theory.24-pushouts.html#21394" class="Bound">l</a> <a id="21463" href="foundation-core.homotopies.html#1877" class="Function Operator">·l</a> <a id="21466" href="synthetic-homotopy-theory.24-pushouts.html#21384" class="Bound">H</a><a id="21467" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="21469" href="foundation-core.homotopies.html#1167" class="Function Operator">∙h</a> <a id="21472" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="21473" href="synthetic-homotopy-theory.24-pushouts.html#21404" class="Bound">K</a> <a id="21475" href="foundation-core.homotopies.html#2083" class="Function Operator">·r</a> <a id="21478" href="synthetic-homotopy-theory.24-pushouts.html#21364" class="Bound">i</a><a id="21479" class="Symbol">)))</a>

<a id="21484" class="Comment">{-
is-pushout-rectangle-is-pushout-right-square :
  ( l : Level) { l1 l2 l3 l4 l5 l6 : Level}
  { A : UU l1} {B : UU l2} {C : UU l3} {X : UU l4} {Y : UU l5} {Z : UU l6}
  ( f : A → X) (i : A → B) (k : B → C) →
  ( c : cocone f i Y) (d : cocone (pr1 (pr2 c)) k Z) →
  universal-property-pushout l f i c →
  universal-property-pushout l (pr1 (pr2 c)) k d →
  universal-property-pushout l f (k ∘ i) (cocone-compose-horizontal f i k c d)
is-pushout-rectangle-is-pushout-right-square l f i k c d up-Y up-Z =
  universal-property-pushout-pullback-property-pushout l f (k ∘ i)
    ( cocone-compose-horizontal f i k c d)
    ( λ T → is-pullback-htpy {!!} {!!} {!!} {!!} {!!} {!!} {!!})
-}</a>

<a id="26921" class="Comment">-- Exercise 16.2</a>

<a id="26939" class="Comment">-- ev-disjunction :</a>
<a id="26959" class="Comment">--   {l1 l2 l3 : Level} (P : UU-Prop l1) (Q : UU-Prop l2) (R : UU-Prop l3) →</a>
<a id="27036" class="Comment">--   ((type-Prop P) * (type-Prop Q) → (type-Prop R)) →</a>
<a id="27091" class="Comment">--   (type-Prop P → type-Prop R) × (type-Prop Q → type-Prop R)</a>
<a id="27154" class="Comment">-- ev-disjunction P Q R f =</a>
<a id="27182" class="Comment">--   pair</a>
<a id="27192" class="Comment">--     ( f ∘ (inl-join (type-Prop P) (type-Prop Q)))</a>
<a id="27245" class="Comment">--     ( f ∘ (inr-join (type-Prop P) (type-Prop Q)))</a>

<a id="27299" class="Comment">-- comparison-ev-disjunction :</a>
<a id="27330" class="Comment">--   {l1 l2 l3 : Level} (P : UU-Prop l1) (Q : UU-Prop l2) (R : UU-Prop l3) →</a>
<a id="27407" class="Comment">--   cocone-join (type-Prop P) (type-Prop Q) (type-Prop R)</a>

<a id="27467" class="Comment">-- universal-property-disjunction-join-prop :</a>
<a id="27513" class="Comment">--   {l1 l2 l3 : Level} (P : UU-Prop l1) (Q : UU-Prop l2) (R : UU-Prop l3) →</a>
<a id="27590" class="Comment">--   is-equiv (ev-disjunction P Q R)</a>
</pre>
